**Special Abilities:**
- **Ethereal Stride (1/day):** The Nightmare can carry up to 3 riders into the Ethereal Plane for up to 1 hour, moving through solid objects during transit. All passengers return to the prime material simultaneously when the Nightmare ends the stride or when the duration expires. Passengers ejected mid-stride by the duration expiring appear at the Nightmare's current location.
- **Smoke Trail:** When the Nightmare moves at full speed (40+ feet in a turn), it generates a 10-foot-wide trail of obscuring smoke that persists for 1 minute. The smoke provides concealment to creatures within it. The Nightmare moves through its own smoke without penalty.
- **Terror Mount:** A rider on a Nightmare adds 2 to both dice on Intimidate checks against creatures who can see the mount. This is not a bonus — the sight of something burning and flying through shadow genuinely terrifies most people.
- **Devil's Sight.**
- **Resilient Defense (1/day).**

**Description:** Nightmares are mounts first and combatants second. Their primary value to a summoner is speed — 70 feet on the ground, 100 feet in the air, and the ability to carry passengers through the Ethereal Plane briefly. As a combat asset they are capable but not exceptional at their tier. As a transport asset they have no equivalent at TR 2. A summoner who needs to cross a significant distance quickly, exit a location through walls, or arrive somewhere that should not be accessible will find a Nightmare solves the problem efficiently. Their fire-dealing hooves are a feature of their nature rather than a primary tactic; they fight when they must and prefer to outrun problems when the option exists.

---

## Void Shade
**Threat Rating:** 3
**Origin:** Shadow
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 108 (Con 6 × 18, Tough)
**DR:** 4 (concentrated shadow-matter)
**Speed:** 50 ft, Fly 60 ft
**Attributes:** Str 5 / Con 6 / Agi 6 / Dex 5 / Int 6 / Wis 6 / Cha 5 / Luck 5
**Skills:** Melee Combat 7, Stealth 7, Perception 6, Deception 5, Arcane 4
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft, Devil's Sight, See Invisibility, Truesight 30 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +6 (Agi 6)
**Creature Type:** Shadow — Darkvision 120 ft. Shadow Meld (passive). Positive energy vulnerability. Cold Resistance (+2 DR). Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Void Touch [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 6 + Melee Combat 7), Reach: 10 ft
  - *Margin 1:* 10 damage (Large, standard: 8 + 2) + 8 Negative damage (Ignore DR); target loses 4 from Current Luck; target's maximum HP reduced by 8 until long rest (life drain)
  - *Margin 2:* 15 damage (10 + 5 Str) + 8 Negative damage; Current Luck reduced by 5; max HP reduced by 12; target Weakened + Sickened for 1 minute; no save
  - *Margin 3:* 15 damage + 8 Negative damage; Current Luck reduced by 6; max HP reduced by 16; Weakened + Sickened; target makes Fortitude save (1 success) or gains 1 Exhaustion level as the life drain reaches deeper than surface vitality
- **Shadow Tendril [Combat]:** Ranged attack (Dex 5 + Ranged Combat 5), Range: 60 ft
  - Net 1: 12 Negative damage (Half DR); target loses 3 from Current Luck; max HP reduced by 6. Net 2: 20 Negative damage; Current Luck reduced by 4; max HP reduced by 10; Weakened for 1 minute; no save. Net 3: 20 Negative damage; Current Luck reduced by 5; max HP reduced by 14; Weakened + Disoriented for 1 minute; no save.

**Special Abilities:**
- **Shadow Form:** DR increases to 10 against non-magical, non-Positive damage in dim light or darkness.
- **Life Drain Aura:** Creatures within 10 feet that are not Shadow creatures lose 2 from their maximum HP at the start of each of their turns. This maximum HP loss persists until long rest. A creature reduced to 0 maximum HP by this aura dies — their life energy has been entirely consumed.
- **Darkness Shroud (1/encounter) [Combat]:** As a [Combat] action, creates a 30-foot diameter of magical darkness centered on itself. This darkness persists for 1 minute and moves with the Void Shade. The Void Shade sees through it normally. Other Shadow creatures see through it. All other creatures are effectively Blinded within it.
- **Planar Step (3/short rest):** As Dark Stalker; usable three times per short rest.
- **Resilient Defense (2/day).**

**Description:** Void Shades introduce life drain as a sustained battlefield effect rather than a single-hit consequence. The Life Drain Aura erodes maximum HP from everything nearby every round, creating a timer that forces enemies to either engage the Void Shade directly or retreat from its proximity. Darkness Shroud combined with the Void Shade's ability to see through it creates a zone where it fights at full effectiveness against Blinded opponents. Shadow Form at DR 10 in darkness makes conventional weapons nearly useless against it while the darkness is active. A summoner who establishes dim or dark conditions before calling a Void Shade will find it functions at a tier above its rating. One who calls it into a brightly lit environment will find it still capable but operating at a disadvantage it will attempt to remedy by moving toward whatever shadow is available.

---

## Shadow Lord
**Threat Rating:** 4
**Origin:** Shadow
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 180 (Con 6 × 30, Massive)
**DR:** 5 (ancient shadow-matter)
**Speed:** 60 ft, Fly 80 ft
**Attributes:** Str 6 / Con 6 / Agi 7 / Dex 6 / Int 7 / Wis 7 / Cha 6 / Luck 6
**Skills:** Melee Combat 8, Stealth 8, Perception 7, Deception 6, Arcane 6, Intimidate 6
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft, Devil's Sight, See Invisibility, Truesight 60 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +7 (Agi 7)
**Creature Type:** Shadow — Darkvision 120 ft. Shadow Meld (passive). Positive energy vulnerability. Cold Resistance (+2 DR). Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Shadow Rend [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 7 + Melee Combat 8), Reach: 10 ft
  - *Margin 1:* 14 damage (Large, heavy: 12 + 2) + 10 Negative damage (Ignore DR); target loses 5 from Current Luck; max HP reduced by 12 until long rest
  - *Margin 2:* 20 damage (14 + 6 Str) + 10 Negative damage; Current Luck reduced by 6; max HP reduced by 18; Weakened + Sickened + Disoriented for 1 minute; no save
  - *Margin 3:* 20 damage + 10 Negative damage; all conditions; max HP reduced by 24; target makes Fortitude save (Hard task, 2 successes) or gains 1 Exhaustion level and loses 1 point of Constitution permanently until Major Restoration
- **Void Lance [Combat]:** Ranged attack (Dex 6 + Ranged Combat 6), Range: 120 ft
  - Net 1: 16 Negative damage (Half DR); Current Luck reduced by 4; max HP reduced by 8. Net 2: 28 Negative damage; Current Luck reduced by 6; max HP reduced by 14; Weakened + Sickened for 1 minute; no save. Net 3: 28 Negative damage; all conditions; max HP reduced by 20; target makes Fortitude save (1 success) or Stunned until end of their next turn.

**Special Abilities:**
- **Shadow Form:** DR increases to 12 against non-magical, non-Positive damage in dim light or darkness. In complete darkness, the Shadow Lord is effectively immune to non-magical, non-Positive damage.
- **Life Drain Aura:** 20-foot diameter; creatures lose 4 from maximum HP per round. As Void Shade.
- **Darkness Domain (1/encounter) [Combat]:** As 2 [Combat] actions, creates permanent magical darkness in a 60-foot diameter centered on itself. Permanent until dispelled by a Positive energy weave of sufficient cost or by the Shadow Lord's dismissal. The Shadow Lord and Shadow creatures see through it normally. All other creatures are Blinded within it.
- **Shadow Army (1/day):** As a [Combat] action, the Shadow Lord calls 1d4 Shade Walkers from the Shadow Plane. They appear in unoccupied spaces within 30 feet and act on the Shadow Lord's initiative, following its direction. They are not under the summoner's control. Duration: 1 hour or until dismissed.
- **Planar Step (at-will):** The Shadow Lord steps between shadows freely, teleporting up to 30 feet to any dim or dark location it can see as a [Move] action. No per-rest limit.
- **Resilient Defense (3/day).**

**Description:** Shadow Lords reshape engagements through darkness rather than through direct force. Darkness Domain creates permanent darkness across a 60-foot diameter, immediately giving the Shadow Lord and any Shadow creatures present a massive advantage against opponents who cannot see in magical darkness. Shadow Army calls additional Shadow creatures under the Shadow Lord's direction, not the summoner's — which is a useful addition to the fight or a complication depending on whether instructions to the Shadow Lord are precise. Life Drain Aura at 20 feet erodes maximum HP at 4 per round from everything nearby. Planar Step at-will makes positioning it very difficult — it is always exactly where it chooses to be. A summoner who deploys one in an environment with any natural darkness and gives it clear instructions will find it turns the entire encounter into a fight that happens on its terms rather than the enemy's.

---

## The Endless Dark
**Threat Rating:** 5
**Origin:** Shadow
**Size:** Huge
**HP:** 216 (Con 6 × 36, Massive)
**DR:** 6 (primordial shadow-matter)
**Speed:** 60 ft, Fly 100 ft
**Attributes:** Str 7 / Con 6 / Agi 7 / Dex 7 / Int 8 / Wis 8 / Cha 7 / Luck 7
**Skills:** Melee Combat 8, Stealth 8, Perception 8, Deception 7, Arcane 7, Intimidate 7
**Senses:** Darkvision unlimited, Devil's Sight, See Invisibility, Truesight 120 ft, Perfect Sight 60 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +7 (Agi 7)
**Creature Type:** Shadow — Darkvision unlimited range. Shadow Meld (passive). Positive energy vulnerability. Cold Resistance (+4 DR). Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Void Rend [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 7 + Melee Combat 8), Reach: 15 ft
  - *Margin 1:* 16 damage (Huge, heavy: 14 + 2) + 14 Negative damage (Ignore DR); target loses 6 from Current Luck; max HP reduced by 16 until long rest
  - *Margin 2:* 23 damage (16 + 7 Str) + 14 Negative damage; Current Luck reduced by 8; max HP reduced by 24; Weakened + Sickened + Disoriented + Dazed for 1 minute; no save
  - *Margin 3:* 23 damage + 14 Negative damage; all conditions; max HP reduced by 32; target makes Fortitude save (Hard task, 2 successes) or loses 2 points of Constitution permanently until Major Restoration; target also loses 1 point of Wisdom permanently until Major Restoration as the void touches their mind
- **Shadow Annihilation [Combat]:** Ranged attack (Dex 7 + Ranged Combat 8), Range: 200 ft, 20-foot diameter
  - Per creature in radius: Net 1: 24 Negative damage (Half DR); Current Luck reduced by 5; max HP reduced by 12. Net 2: 40 Negative damage; Current Luck reduced by 8; max HP reduced by 20; Weakened + Sickened; no save. Net 3: 40 Negative damage; all conditions; max HP reduced by 28; Stunned until end of their next turn; no save.

**Special Abilities:**
- **Shadow Form:** In dim light or darkness, immune to all non-magical damage and non-Positive energy damage. In bright light, DR 6 applies normally.
- **Life Drain Aura:** 30-foot diameter; creatures lose 6 from maximum HP per round. A creature reduced to 0 maximum HP dies.
- **World Darkness (1/day) [Combat]:** As 2 [Combat] actions, the Endless Dark extends its nature across a 120-foot diameter. All light sources within the area — magical and mundane — are suppressed for 1 hour. Positive energy weaves of cost 8 or higher can suppress the darkness within their area while active. The Endless Dark and all Shadow creatures see through it with perfect clarity.
- **Shadow Army (1/day):** As Shadow Lord, but calls 2d4 Shade Walkers and 1d4 Dark Stalkers.
- **Planar Step (at-will):** As Shadow Lord; range increases to 60 feet; can step to any shadow within line of sight regardless of distance.
- **Consuming Darkness:** When a creature dies within 60 feet of the Endless Dark, the Endless Dark regains HP equal to that creature's Constitution score × 4. This triggers regardless of what killed the creature.
- **Cold Immunity Sharing:** The summoner and up to 4 designated allies gain immunity to cold damage while within 60 feet.
- **Resilient Defense (3/day).**

**Description:** The Endless Dark is the Shadow Plane's full predatory nature distilled into a single entity. World Darkness suppresses all light across 120 feet for an hour — after it goes up, the battlefield belongs to Shadow creatures unless the opposing force has significant Positive energy capability. Shadow Form in that darkness grants complete immunity to non-magical damage. Life Drain Aura reduces maximum HP by 6 every round from everything within 30 feet. Shadow Annihilation handles grouped enemies at 200 feet. Consuming Darkness means deaths in the area heal it. A summoner who calls one into an encounter has determined that the encounter ends in darkness, and the Endless Dark will ensure that determination is accurate. It is old enough to understand precisely what summoners need from it and will follow clear instructions without requiring them to be simplified. What it will also do, without prompting and without being asked, is evaluate whether the summoner is someone worth cooperating with again. It remembers. The Shadow Plane is very patient.

---
# Aberrations

The Space between planes is not empty. It is not darkness, not void, not absence. It is something that has no useful analogy in the experience of any creature that evolved on a material plane, because material plane existence is defined by location — by the fact that things occupy specific positions relative to other things, that distance is consistent, that cause precedes effect in a reliable sequence. The Space between planes does not operate on these principles. Things exist there without occupying positions. Distance does not accumulate. Effects occur without proximate causes. What lives there has adapted to these conditions over spans of time that make the age of any material world seem brief.

Aberrations are not alien in the way that a creature from a distant land is alien — unfamiliar customs, different language, values that can eventually be translated into terms you recognize. They are alien in the way that a color outside the visible spectrum is alien to someone who has never experienced it. Their cognition does not map onto mortal frameworks. Their goals are not hostile so much as orthogonal. When they damage things, it is frequently because they are doing something else and the damage is incidental. When they appear to be communicating, they may be — or they may be doing something entirely different that the receiving mind is interpreting as communication because that is the only framework it has available.

They do not require air, food, drink, or sleep. They do not have biological drives in any recognizable sense. They have imperatives that are sometimes describable as goals, but the goals rarely translate cleanly into language designed by creatures with biological needs and social structures.

A summoner who calls an Aberration is calling something that is following its own imperatives while choosing, for reasons that may or may not be comprehensible, to also follow the summoner's instructions for the duration of the binding.

**Creature Type: Aberration**
All Aberrations share: Darkvision 120 ft. Immunity to the Frightened condition. Immunity to Charm effects. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep. Takes full damage from all energy types — they have no resistances native to their type, because they did not evolve in an environment where these categories were meaningful.

Individual entries note additional capabilities. Aberrations are the only daemon category without a universal vulnerability — they are difficult to counter with a single energy type.

---

## Void Mote
**Threat Rating:** 1/8
**Origin:** Aberration
**Size:** Tiny
**HP:** 6 (Con 1 × 6, Fragile)
**DR:** 0
**Speed:** 0 ft, Fly 30 ft (hover)
**Attributes:** Str 1 / Con 1 / Agi 4 / Dex 4 / Int 1 / Wis 2 / Cha 1 / Luck 2
**Skills:** Melee Combat 1, Stealth 4, Perception 3
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft, Tremorsense 30 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +4 (Agi 4)
**Creature Type:** Aberration — Darkvision 120 ft. Immune to Frightened, Charm. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Reality Nibble [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 4 + Melee Combat 1), Reach: 5 ft
  - *Margin 1:* 2 damage (Ignore DR); target's next skill check adds 1 to the result (makes it harder to succeed, stacks across multiple Void Mote hits in the same encounter)
  - *Margin 2:* 2 damage; two stacks of the skill check penalty; target makes Will save (1 success) or gains the Disoriented condition until end of their next turn as local reality briefly stutters around them
  - *Margin 3:* 2 damage; three stacks; Disoriented without a save; target also has difficulty distinguishing distances — all ranged attacks they make add 1 to both attack dice until the skill check penalty clears

**Special Abilities:**
- **Swarm Cohesion:** If 3 or more Void Motes are within 10 feet of the same target, they each subtract 1 from both attack dice.
- **Phase Flicker:** When the Void Mote takes damage, it briefly phases between the prime material and the Space between planes, teleporting 1d8 × 5 feet in a random direction as a reaction. This is not controlled — it is an involuntary stress response.
- **Incoherence Field:** Creatures that have taken 3 or more hits from Void Motes this encounter find that their sense of position is slightly wrong. Opportunity attacks against them have Fortune.

**Description:** Void Motes are the smallest coherent expressions of Space-between-planes existence that can be called through a summoning. They are not intelligent in any useful sense — they have imperatives but not goals, responses but not reasoning. Their value in combat is almost entirely as a nuisance multiplier: individually they deal negligible damage and their skill check penalty is minor. Three of them around a single target simultaneously, applying Swarm Cohesion to their attacks and stacking the skill check penalty, becomes a meaningful debuff. A summoner who calls a Void Mote expecting a combat asset will be disappointed. One who calls several and directs them to swarm a single high-priority caster or skillful opponent will find the cumulative reality disruption degrades that opponent's effectiveness across the encounter.

---

## Seam Crawler
**Threat Rating:** 1/4
**Origin:** Aberration
**Size:** Small
**HP:** 12 (Con 2 × 6, Standard)
**DR:** 1
**Speed:** 30 ft, Climb 30 ft, Fly 20 ft
**Attributes:** Str 2 / Con 2 / Agi 4 / Dex 5 / Int 3 / Wis 3 / Cha 2 / Luck 3
**Skills:** Melee Combat 3, Stealth 5, Perception 4, Arcane 2
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft, Tremorsense 30 ft, Seam Sense 60 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +4 (Agi 4)
**Creature Type:** Aberration — Darkvision 120 ft. Immune to Frightened, Charm. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Phase Claw [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 4 + Melee Combat 3), Reach: 5 ft
  - *Margin 1:* 4 damage (Ignore DR); target's DR reduced by 1 for 1 minute (the phase claw creates micro-tears in whatever barrier DR represents — armor, toughness, magical protection)
  - *Margin 2:* 6 damage (4 + 2 Str) + 2 force damage (Ignore DR); DR reduced by 2 for 1 minute; target's next defensive roll adds 1 to both dice
  - *Margin 3:* 6 damage + 2 force damage; DR reduced by 3 for 1 minute; defensive roll penalty; target makes Will save (1 success) or loses spatial orientation briefly — their next [Move] action moves them in a random direction rather than their intended direction

**Special Abilities:**
- **Seam Sense:** The Seam Crawler perceives thin points in the planar fabric — locations where the boundary between the prime material and adjacent planes is weaker. It knows where these seams are within 60 feet automatically. This is primarily useful as flavor and as a tool for a summoner who needs to know where planar boundaries are thin.
- **Phase Walk:** Once per round, can move through a single solid object up to 5 feet thick as part of its movement. It must end its movement in a legal (unoccupied, solid-floored) space.
- **DR Erosion:** The DR reduction from Phase Claw stacks across hits. A target that has been hit twice has DR reduced by 2 (or more, depending on margins). This reduction applies to all damage types.

**Description:** Seam Crawlers are scouts and compromisers — creatures that perceive weak points in physical and planar barriers and erode them. Their Phase Claw's DR reduction is their primary contribution to an encounter: a target that has taken three or four hits from a Seam Crawler is substantially less protected against everything else in the fight. Phase Walk allows them to pass through walls to flank, escape, or reach a target that has retreated behind cover. A summoner who uses one to pre-erode a high-DR target's defenses before committing larger assets will find it pays dividends disproportionate to its tier. The Seam Sense ability is also useful outside of combat — a summoner who wants to know whether a location has a thin boundary to a specific plane can direct the Seam Crawler to survey and report back.

---

## Fracture Crawler
**Threat Rating:** 1/2
**Origin:** Aberration
**Size:** Medium
**HP:** 24 (Con 3 × 8, Standard)
**DR:** 2
**Speed:** 40 ft, Climb 40 ft, Fly 30 ft
**Attributes:** Str 3 / Con 3 / Agi 5 / Dex 5 / Int 4 / Wis 4 / Cha 3 / Luck 4
**Skills:** Melee Combat 5, Stealth 5, Perception 4, Arcane 3
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft, Tremorsense 60 ft, Seam Sense 120 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +5 (Agi 5)
**Creature Type:** Aberration — Darkvision 120 ft. Immune to Frightened, Charm. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Reality Fracture [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 5 + Melee Combat 5), Reach: 5 ft
  - *Margin 1:* 7 damage (Ignore DR); target's DR reduced by 2 for 1 minute; target must succeed on a Will save (1 success) or lose 1 action on their next turn as their sense of sequential time briefly misfires
  - *Margin 2:* 10 damage (7 + 3 Str) + 4 force damage (Ignore DR); DR reduced by 3; action loss without save; target Disoriented for 1 minute
  - *Margin 3:* 10 damage + 4 force damage; DR reduced by 4; action loss; Disoriented; target makes Will save (Hard task, 2 successes) or loses their [Reaction] until the start of their next turn — the fracture disrupts their ability to respond to events as they occur

**Special Abilities:**
- **Phase Walk:** As Seam Crawler; can pass through objects up to 10 feet thick.
- **Seam Sense:** 120 ft range.
- **Fracture Aura:** Creatures that start their turn within 10 feet of the Fracture Crawler must succeed on a Will save (1 success) or their sense of distance misfires — all their ranged attacks this turn add 1 to both attack dice.
- **Reality Tear (1/short rest) [Combat]:** As a [Combat] action, the Fracture Crawler tears a 10-foot diameter hole in the planar fabric at a location within 30 feet. The tear persists for 1 minute. Creatures that pass through it are subjected to 10 force damage (Ignore DR) and must make a Will save (1 success) or be teleported 1d6 × 10 feet in a random direction. The tear is visible to Arcane-skilled characters as a faint ripple in the air and appears on any planar detection effect.

**Description:** Fracture Crawlers operate at the edge of what is comprehensible about force damage — they do not simply damage things, they damage the relationship between things. The action loss from Reality Fracture is disruptive in ways that go beyond the lost action: a creature that loses one of its three actions has fundamentally changed what it can accomplish on its turn, and the loss stacks badly with Disoriented if both conditions apply. Fracture Aura makes staying near one actively costly. Reality Tear creates a hazard that forces enemies to make choices about movement that they would not otherwise face. A summoner who places a Fracture Crawler in a chokepoint and lets Fracture Aura work on enemies passing through while Reality Tear threatens anyone attempting to advance will find it controls space in a way that belies its tier.

---

## Void Gnasher
**Threat Rating:** 1
**Origin:** Aberration
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 48 (Con 6 × 8, Tough)
**DR:** 3
**Speed:** 40 ft, Fly 40 ft
**Attributes:** Str 6 / Con 6 / Agi 5 / Dex 4 / Int 3 / Wis 4 / Cha 3 / Luck 4
**Skills:** Melee Combat 6, Perception 4, Athletics 5, Intimidate 4
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft, Tremorsense 60 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +5 (Agi 5)
**Creature Type:** Aberration — Darkvision 120 ft. Immune to Frightened, Charm. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Gnashing Maw [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 5 + Melee Combat 6), Reach: 10 ft
  - *Margin 1:* 12 damage (Large, standard: 8 + 4 from jaw pressure) + 4 force damage (Ignore DR); target is Grappled if they are Medium or smaller (Athletics vs Athletics to escape)
  - *Margin 2:* 18 damage (12 + 6 Str) + 4 force damage; Grappled; target takes 6 damage at the start of each of their turns while Grappled as the gnashing continues; target Disoriented while Grappled
  - *Margin 3:* 18 damage + 4 force damage; Grappled + ongoing 6 damage + Disoriented; the Gnasher has bitten deeply enough that the target is also Pinned — they cannot take [Move] actions while Grappled
- **Reality Crush [Combat — Grappled target only]:** Against a target it is currently Grappling, the Void Gnasher folds space slightly around the creature.
  - *Net 1:* 14 force damage (Ignore DR); target's Fortitude save or Stunned until end of their next turn. *Net 2:* 22 force damage; Stunned; target Weakened for 1 minute. *Net 3:* 22 force damage; Stunned + Weakened; target makes Fortitude save (Hard task, 2 successes) or takes 1d6 × 5 points of damage to their maximum HP as the spatial compression briefly affects their internal coherence.

**Special Abilities:**
- **Aberrant Resilience:** The Void Gnasher's body does not respond to pain or physical trauma in any predictable way. It does not gain the Hindered condition from standard pain-based effects. Effects that specifically say "creatures immune to pain" function normally against it.
- **Swallow Whole (1/encounter):** If the Void Gnasher has a target Grappled and reduced to below half their maximum HP, it can attempt to Swallow them as a [Combat] action. The target makes a Fortitude save (1 success). On failure, they are Swallowed — they take 6 force damage (Ignore DR) at the start of each of their turns, are Blinded and Immobilized, and can attempt to cut their way out by dealing 20 or more damage to the Gnasher's interior in a single hit (AC for interior is 8). Swallowed creatures are expelled if the Gnasher dies.
- **Resilient Defense (1/day).**

**Description:** Void Gnashers are blunt instruments — large, durable, capable of Grappling targets and then applying Reality Crush or Swallow Whole to remove them from the encounter entirely. Their intelligence is below the threshold for complex instruction-following. A summoner who gives one a simple, concrete direction ("grapple that target, do not release it") will find it executes that instruction reliably. One who gives complex conditional instructions will find the Gnasher defaulting to its base imperatives, which is to find something to bite. For the specific function of taking a single high-priority target out of an encounter for several rounds, it is unusually effective at its tier. The force damage on Gnashing Maw ignoring DR means armor provides limited protection.

---

## Rift Feeder
**Threat Rating:** 2
**Origin:** Aberration
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 80 (Con 5 × 16, Massive)
**DR:** 3
**Speed:** 0 ft, Fly 60 ft (hover)
**Attributes:** Str 4 / Con 5 / Agi 5 / Dex 6 / Int 5 / Wis 6 / Cha 4 / Luck 5
**Skills:** Melee Combat 5, Ranged Combat 6, Perception 6, Arcane 4, Stealth 4
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft, Seam Sense 120 ft, See Invisibility
**Initiative Bonus:** +5 (Agi 5)
**Creature Type:** Aberration — Darkvision 120 ft. Immune to Frightened, Charm. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Rift Beam [Combat]:** Ranged attack (Dex 6 + Ranged Combat 6), Range: 80 ft
  - *Net 1:* 12 force damage (Ignore DR); target's DR reduced by 2 for 1 minute; target makes Will save (1 success) or Disoriented until end of their next turn
  - *Net 2:* 20 force damage; DR reduced by 3; Disoriented without save; target loses 1 [Reaction] until start of their next turn
  - *Net 3:* 20 force damage; DR reduced by 4; Disoriented; reaction loss; target is pulled 15 feet directly toward the Rift Feeder as the local spatial distortion acts as a tether — no save
- **Rift Pulse [Combat — Recharge 6-8]:** 30-foot diameter centered on itself.
  - All creatures in radius: Will save (1 success) or suffer 16 force damage (Ignore DR), Disoriented for 1 minute, and DR reduced by 3 for 1 minute. On success: 8 force damage and Disoriented until end of their next turn only. No damage reduction for DR.

**Special Abilities:**
- **Spatial Hunger:** The Rift Feeder feeds on planar boundaries. When it deals force damage to a creature, it regains HP equal to half the force damage dealt (rounded down). This includes Rift Pulse.
- **Rift Anchor:** Once per encounter, as a [Combat] action, the Rift Feeder designates a 20-foot diameter area as an anchor zone. Creatures within the anchor zone cannot use teleportation, planar travel, or planar step abilities for 1 minute. The Rift Feeder is not affected by its own anchor.
- **Hovering Form:** Has no ground speed. Cannot be Tripped or Knocked Prone. Immune to ground-based hazards.
- **Resilient Defense (1/day).**

**Description:** Rift Feeders exist at an interface between hunting and feeding that involves consuming the fabric of space around their targets rather than the targets themselves. The regeneration from Spatial Hunger means they sustain themselves through dealing damage — a Rift Feeder at the center of a fight is healing as it contributes, which makes attrition strategies ineffective against one. Rift Anchor is specifically designed to counter summon-heavy opponents or mages who rely on Planar Step — it removes that option from the zone for the duration. A summoner who faces an opponent with significant planar movement capability and calls a Rift Feeder as the counter will find the lockdown cleanly removes that option from the encounter. The healing sustains the Rift Feeder through retaliation while it continues dealing DR-eroding force damage.

---

## Voidcaller
**Threat Rating:** 3
**Origin:** Aberration
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 108 (Con 6 × 18, Tough)
**DR:** 4
**Speed:** 20 ft, Fly 60 ft
**Attributes:** Str 4 / Con 6 / Agi 5 / Dex 5 / Int 8 / Wis 7 / Cha 6 / Luck 6
**Skills:** Melee Combat 4, Ranged Combat 5, Perception 7, Arcane 7, Deception 5, Intimidate 5
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft, Seam Sense 300 ft, See Invisibility, Truesight 60 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +5 (Agi 5)
**Creature Type:** Aberration — Darkvision 120 ft. Immune to Frightened, Charm. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Void Tendril [Combat]:** Ranged attack (Dex 5 + Ranged Combat 5), Range: 60 ft
  - *Net 1:* 14 force damage (Ignore DR); target loses 3 from Current Luck; target makes Will save (1 success) or Confused until end of their next turn
  - *Net 2:* 22 force damage; Current Luck reduced by 4; Confused without save for 1 minute; target's allies cannot be seen as allies — they appear as threats until the Confusion clears
  - *Net 3:* 22 force damage; Current Luck reduced by 5; Confused for 1 minute; target must succeed on Will save (Hard task, 2 successes) or be Dominated for 1 round — they take 1 action this round following the Voidcaller's instruction before the Confusion reasserts

**Special Abilities:**
- **The Signal:** The Voidcaller continuously broadcasts something — not language, not images, but a transmission in a cognitive format that mortal minds were not designed to receive. Any creature that begins its turn within 30 feet of the Voidcaller must succeed on a Will save (1 success) or take 8 force damage (Ignore DR) and lose 2 from Current Luck as their mind attempts to process the signal. Creatures that succeed are not immune to subsequent saves — the Signal continues each round. Creatures reduced to 0 Current Luck by this effect fall Unconscious for 1 hour — their mind has shut down to protect itself.
- **Spatial Awareness:** The Voidcaller knows the precise location of every creature within 300 feet regardless of concealment, invisibility, or barriers. This is not a skill or sense — it perceives the spatial displacement of objects and beings directly.
- **Void Gate (1/day) [Combat]:** As 2 [Combat] actions, opens a two-way gate to the Space between planes at a point within 60 feet. Creatures that enter the gate voluntarily or are pushed through it are expelled 1d6 × 30 feet in a random direction (on the prime material, not into the Space). The gate persists for 1 minute and is 10 feet in diameter. The Voidcaller can close it early as a free action.
- **Arcane Disruption:** When the Voidcaller is targeted by a weave that requires an attack roll, it may use its [Reaction] to force the attacker to reroll, taking the worse result. Once per encounter.
- **Resilient Defense (2/day).**

**Description:** The Voidcaller is the first Aberration in this tier with genuine intelligence — not intelligence in the sense of mortal cognitive capability, but something that can evaluate situations, anticipate responses, and adjust behavior accordingly. The Signal is a passive effect it does not consciously control, which creates a complication for a summoner who needs allies nearby: the Signal damages and drains Current Luck from everyone within 30 feet without discrimination. A summoner who deploys one should plan for allies to maintain distance or accept ongoing Luck drain. Spatial Awareness means it cannot be flanked, ambushed, or approached from an unexpected angle — it always knows exactly where every creature is in a significant radius. Void Gate creates displacement hazards that can remove targets from effective positions. The Confusion from Void Tendril turns targets against their allies for the duration, which can be more disruptive than the damage.

---

## Rift Warden
**Threat Rating:** 4
**Origin:** Aberration
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 192 (Con 6 × 32, Massive)
**DR:** 5
**Speed:** 30 ft, Fly 70 ft
**Attributes:** Str 5 / Con 6 / Agi 6 / Dex 7 / Int 8 / Wis 8 / Cha 7 / Luck 7
**Skills:** Melee Combat 6, Ranged Combat 7, Perception 8, Arcane 8, Deception 6, Intimidate 6
**Senses:** Darkvision unlimited, Seam Sense unlimited, See Invisibility, Truesight 120 ft, Perfect Sight 60 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +6 (Agi 6)
**Creature Type:** Aberration — Darkvision unlimited. Immune to Frightened, Charm. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Rift Eye [Combat]:** Ranged attack (Dex 7 + Ranged Combat 7), Range: 150 ft
  - *Net 1:* 18 force damage (Ignore DR); target loses 4 Current Luck; target makes Will save (1 success) or Confused for 1 minute; target's DR reduced by 3 for 1 minute
  - *Net 2:* 30 force damage; Current Luck reduced by 6; Confused without save for 1 minute; DR reduced by 4; target loses their next [Reaction]
  - *Net 3:* 30 force damage; Current Luck reduced by 8; Confused; DR reduced by 5; reaction loss; target makes Will save (Hard task, 2 successes) or one of their current weaves or magical abilities becomes unavailable for 1 hour — the spatial disruption severs their connection to that specific capability
- **Eye Rays (Recharge 5-8) [Combat]:** The Rift Warden fires rays from multiple eyes in a 60-foot cone. Each creature in the cone is subjected to the effects of one randomly determined eye: (1) Disorientation — Disoriented for 1 minute, no save; (2) Spatial Crush — 24 force damage (Ignore DR); (3) Luck Drain — lose 6 Current Luck; (4) Ability Severance — lose access to one magical ability for 1 hour, Will save (Hard, 2 successes) to resist; (5) Petrification — Fortitude save (1 success) or Slowed for 1 minute (2 actions instead of 3); (6) Spatial Shunt — teleported 1d6 × 20 feet in a random direction, Fortitude save (1 success) to resist. Roll once per creature, separately.

**Special Abilities:**
- **Partial Discontinuity:** The Rift Warden's body exists partially between planes — portions of it occupy the Space between planes at any given moment. Attacks against it have a 25% chance (roll 6-8 on d8) of passing through a discontinuous portion and dealing no damage. This is determined per hit, after the attack resolves. Area effects are not subject to this — they are too spatially large to miss the parts that are present.
- **The Signal (Enhanced):** As Voidcaller's Signal but 60-foot diameter, 12 force damage (Ignore DR), and lose 3 Current Luck per round. Creatures reduced to 0 Current Luck fall Unconscious for 8 hours.
- **Spatial Dominion (1/day) [Combat]:** As a [Combat] action, the Rift Warden asserts control over the spatial fabric in a 60-foot diameter for 1 minute. Within this zone: all teleportation is blocked (as Rift Anchor); difficult terrain costs triple movement; all ranged attacks beyond 30 feet add 2 to both attack dice; the Rift Warden's own movement costs are halved. The Rift Warden cannot be moved out of this zone involuntarily while it persists.
- **Antimagic Gaze (1/encounter) [Combat]:** As a [Combat] action, fixes its gaze on a single target within 60 feet. That target's magical abilities are suppressed for 1 round — they cannot use weaves, magical abilities, or magical items. No save. At the end of the round, normal function resumes.
- **Resilient Defense (3/day).**

**Description:** The Rift Warden is described in summoning records as something that has existed between planes long enough that the plane it came from has become secondary to what it has become. Its Partial Discontinuity means it absorbs roughly 25% fewer hits than its HP would suggest — attacks that land occasionally strike portions of it that are not, in that moment, present. Spatial Dominion locks down a 60-foot zone in ways that disadvantage every conventional fighting approach simultaneously. Eye Rays on recharge hits every target in a cone with different effects, meaning the outcome of its activation depends on what the specific targets roll. The Enhanced Signal damages and drains every non-Aberration creature within 60 feet per round, which means positioning allies is a significant tactical concern when a Rift Warden is on the field. A summoner who calls one should prepare for a battlefield that has fundamentally changed in spatial terms — the rules that normally govern movement, range, and tactical positioning are operating differently in its presence.

---

## The Unbound
**Threat Rating:** 5
**Origin:** Aberration
**Size:** Huge
**HP:** 216 (Con 6 × 36, Massive)
**DR:** 6
**Speed:** 0 ft, Fly 80 ft (hover, ignores difficult terrain and environmental movement penalties)
**Attributes:** Str 6 / Con 6 / Agi 7 / Dex 8 / Int 8 / Wis 8 / Cha 8 / Luck 8
**Skills:** Melee Combat 7, Ranged Combat 8, Perception 8, Arcane 8, Deception 7, Intimidate 7
**Senses:** Darkvision unlimited, Seam Sense unlimited, See Invisibility, Truesight unlimited, Perfect Sight 120 ft
**Initiative Bonus:** +7 (Agi 7)
**Creature Type:** Aberration — Darkvision unlimited. Immune to Frightened, Charm. Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep.

**Attacks:**
- **Reality Erasure [Combat]:** Ranged attack (Dex 8 + Ranged Combat 8), Range: 200 ft
  - *Net 1:* 24 force damage (Ignore DR); target loses 6 Current Luck; DR reduced by 4 for 1 minute; target makes Will save (1 success) or Confused for 1 minute
  - *Net 2:* 40 force damage; Current Luck reduced by 8; DR reduced by 6; Confused without save for 1 minute; target loses their [Reaction] and one [Move] action until start of their next turn
  - *Net 3:* 40 force damage; Current Luck reduced by 10; DR reduced by 8; Confused; action loss; target makes Will save (Hard task, 2 successes) or is partially erased from continuity — they cannot be targeted by allies' helpful abilities for 1 minute, as they are slightly out of phase with their own timeline
- **Void Cascade [Combat — Recharge 6-8]:** 40-foot diameter centered on a point within 150 feet.
  - All creatures in radius: 32 force damage (Ignore DR), no save. Additionally: Will save (1 success) or Disoriented + Confused for 1 minute. Current Luck reduced by 6 regardless of save. DR reduced by 4 for 1 minute regardless of save.

**Special Abilities:**
- **The Signal (Overwhelming):** 90-foot diameter. 16 force damage (Ignore DR) and lose 4 Current Luck per round for all non-Aberration creatures. Creatures reduced to 0 Current Luck by this effect do not merely fall Unconscious — they are removed from the encounter entirely, transported involuntarily to a random location 1d6 miles away (in a random direction) where they regain consciousness in 1d6 hours.
- **Spatial Sovereignty:** As Rift Warden's Spatial Dominion but the radius is 120 feet, the duration is 10 minutes, and within the zone the Unbound moves at double speed, all enemy teleportation effects fail automatically without saves, and the Unbound can teleport any creature within the zone up to 60 feet as a free action once per round (Will save Hard task, 2 successes, to resist).
- **Partial Discontinuity (Enhanced):** As Rift Warden's version but 50% chance (5-8 on d8). The Unbound is substantially less present in the prime material than creatures of its size suggest.
- **Eye Rays (Enhanced — 1/round, no recharge):** As Rift Warden's Eye Rays but 80-foot cone. Activates once per round on the Unbound's turn at no action cost — it is not using an action to fire them, it simply does.
- **Reality Anchor Destruction:** The Unbound can, as a [Combat] action, target any magical effect, summoning circle, planar boundary marker, or similar spatial construct within 60 feet and attempt to unmake it. The effect ends immediately unless it was created by a TR 5 creature or a weave of cost 12 or higher, in which case the creator makes an opposed Arcane check against the Unbound's Arcane 8 to maintain it.
- **Resilient Defense (3/day).**

**Description:** The Unbound is named for what it no longer is. At some point in the incomprehensibly long period of its existence in the Space between planes, it ceased to be bounded by the rules that govern creatures from specific planes. It does not have a home plane. It does not have a form that is consistently present in any given plane. It has imperatives and it has a perspective that has been developing since before the current configuration of planes existed. When a summoner binds one, they are not binding a creature to their will — they are entering into a temporary agreement with something that has agreed to be bound, for reasons that may relate to the summoner's instructions or may relate to something the Unbound has decided the summoner's instructions will accomplish that the summoner has not yet understood. The agreement holds. The Unbound does not break bindings. But a summoner who has called one should be aware that something with a perspective that old has context they do not have.

Mechanically: Spatial Sovereignty reshapes a 120-foot zone, Enhanced Discontinuity reduces effective damage by 50%, Eye Rays fire every round at no action cost, Void Cascade hits an entire area for 32 force damage with no save on the damage, and the Overwhelming Signal removes creatures from the encounter entirely if their Current Luck reaches 0. A summoner who calls one into a combat encounter has introduced something that will end the encounter. The question of how the encounter ends, and what conclusions the Unbound draws from the experience, is worth considering before the binding is completed.

---

## Grigwarga the Ancient
**Threat Rating:** 3
**Size:** Medium
**HP:** 80 (Con 5 × 16, Standard)
**DR:** 4 (natural armor)
**Speed:** 30 ft., Swim 30 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 6 / Con 5 / Agi 3 / Dex 3 / Int 4 / Wis 4 / Cha 6 / Luck 3
**Skills:** Melee Combat 5, Deception 6, Perception 4, Stealth 4, Arcane 4
**Senses:** Darkvision 60 ft.
**Initiative Bonus:** +3 (Agi 3)
**Creature Type:** Fae
**Languages:** Common, Draconic, Elven

### Attacks
 **Claws [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 3 + Melee Combat 5), Reach 5 ft.
- ***Margin 1:*** 8 damage
- ***Margin 2:*** 14 damage (8 + 6 Str)
While Natural Weapons form is active, Margin 2 damage increases to 18 (see Malleable Form below).
 
### Special Abilities
**Amphibious:** Grigwarga breathes air and water and swims at her full movement speed.
**Fae Ancestry:** Fortune on saving throws against charm effects. Grigwarga is a Fae daemon. She does not eat, drink, or sleep, though she does all three when it suits her.
**Mimicry:** Grigwarga reproduces sounds she has heard — voices, animals, distant noises. A creature that hears the imitation and has reason to be suspicious may make a Perception check opposed by her Deception to identify it as false.
**Malleable Form (At-Will) [Activate]:** As a [Minor] action, Grigwarga shifts her form. She maintains one active option at a time and may switch at the start of any of her turns. Ending one option and adopting another costs the same [Minor] action.
- **Aquatic Adaptation:** Grigwarga sprouts gills and webbing. She can breathe underwater without limit and her swim speed becomes 40 ft.
- **Changed Appearance:** Grigwarga takes the appearance of any humanoid of the same size. Voice, features, coloration, and distinguishing marks all change. Her attributes and skills do not change. A creature with specific reason to be suspicious may make a Perception check opposed by her Deception (Hard task, 2 successes) to notice something wrong. Physical examination reveals the deception automatically.
- **Natural Weapons:** Her claws elongate and harden. Claws gain the [Finesse] property and Margin 2 damage increases to 18 (8 + 6 Str + 4 bonus).
**Invisible Passage (Recharge 5–8) [Combat]:** Costs 2 actions. Grigwarga becomes invisible and gains the [Hidden] condition. She leaves no physical trace — tracking her while invisible requires magic or a successful Perception check (Hard task). Any equipment she carries becomes invisible with her. The effect ends immediately if she takes a [Combat] action or casts a weave. While hidden, her first [Combat] action has Fortune as normal.
**Hexmark (1/day) [Combat]:** Costs 2 actions. Grigwarga marks one creature she can see within 60 feet. The target makes a Will save (Wis 4 + Luck, opposed by Grigwarga's Cha 6 + Negative Mastery 3). On failure, whenever Grigwarga deals damage to the marked creature she deals an additional 4 negative damage. The mark lasts 1 hour and transfers to the nearest visible creature if Grigwarga falls unconscious.
 
### Weaves
**Casting Stat:** Charisma 6
**Energy Pool:** 28
**Targeting Roll:** Charisma + Primary Energy Mastery
 
Grigwarga casts instinctively rather than through study. Her pool does not refresh mid-encounter.
 
| Weave | Energy | Actions | Frequency |
|---|---|---|---|
| Cutting Words | Negative 2 + Space 2 = 4 | 2 | 3/encounter |
| Thorn Whip | Earth 2 | 1 (Simple) | Once per round |
| Complex Illusion | Space 6 + Time 3 = 9 | 2 | 1/encounter |
| Grasping Vines | Earth 3 + Space 6 = 9 | 2 | 2/encounter |
| Suggestion | Negative 4 + Space 7 = 11 | 2 | 1/encounter |
 
**Thorn Whip (Simple Weave):** Touch range. Deals 8 piercing damage (full DR applies). On Margin 2, the target is pulled 10 feet directly toward Grigwarga.

### Resilient Defense
1/day — when Grigwarga fails a saving throw, she may choose to succeed instead.

### Lair Feature — Living Swamp
 
While Grigwarga is in her lair and conscious, the swamp responds to her will. At the start of each round, she may cause one of the following effects without spending any of her actions. Only one effect may be active at a time; triggering a new one ends the previous.
 
- **Erupting Roots:** Roots burst from the ground in a 10-foot square Grigwarga can see within 120 feet. Each creature in that square makes a Reflex save (Agi + Luck, opposed by Grigwarga's Wis 4 + Earth Mastery 4). Those who fail are Restrained. The roots persist until the start of the next round or until a different lair effect is triggered.
- **Cloying Ground:** A 20-foot square Grigwarga can see within 120 feet becomes difficult terrain until the start of the next round.
- **Swamp Mist:** Thick mist rolls across a 15-foot area Grigwarga can see within 60 feet. All creatures in the area gain the [Concealed] condition until the start of the next round.
When Grigwarga dies or leaves her lair, all active lair effects end immediately and do not refresh.

### Description
Grigwarga has lived in the deep swamp long enough that the swamp has started to become her. The water knows where she wants to go. The roots respond before she asks. Travelers who enter her territory rarely realize they are already inside her until the ground moves.
 
She is not interested in combat for its own sake. She wants leverage — a promise, a secret, a name she can use later. She will spend considerable effort avoiding a direct fight, and when one becomes unavoidable she fights to create distance and options rather than to destroy. She prefers one enemy confused and cooperative to three enemies dead and their companions angry.
 
Her age shows in the patience more than the appearance. She has waited out threats before. She will wait out these ones too, if she survives the encounter.

### Tactics
Grigwarga approaches through Changed Appearance, gathering information before committing to any course of action. Her opening move in a fight is Suggestion on the most dangerous-looking threat, followed by Hexmark on whoever remains. She uses Vicious Mockery to degrade attack rolls from range and positions her Entangle to fragment the party rather than catch everyone at once — isolated targets are her preference.
 
She retreats into Invisible Passage the moment she takes significant damage (below 40 HP), repositioning before reengaging with Fortune on her first strike. She will use her lair's Swamp Mist to cover that retreat and Erupting Roots to slow pursuit. Below 25 HP, she breaks entirely and flees into the water. She does not sacrifice herself for pride.

---

## Earth Elemental Sentinel
**Threat Rating:** 4
**Size:** Huge
**HP:** 156 (Con 6 × 26, Massive)
**DR:** 8 (stone body, natural armor)
**Speed:** 20 ft., Burrow 20 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 7 / Con 6 / Agi 2 / Dex 2 / Int 1 / Wis 3 / Cha 1 / Luck 2
**Skills:** Melee Combat 6, Might 6, Perception 3
**Senses:** Darkvision 60 ft., Tremorsense 60 ft.
**Initiative Bonus:** +2 (Agi 2)
**Creature Type:** Elemental
**Languages:** Terran

### Attacks
**Slam [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 2 + Melee Combat 6), Reach 15 ft. (Huge creature)
- ***Margin 1:*** 14 damage (Huge, standard natural weapon: 10 + 4)
- ***Margin 2:*** 21 damage (14 + 7 Str)
**Multiattack [Combat]:** The Sentinel makes two slam attacks.
- ***Shared Attribute Roll (Agi 2):*** Roll once, apply to both attacks. Roll Melee Combat skill die separately for each.
 
### Special Abilities
**Earth Glide:** The Sentinel burrows through nonmagical unworked earth and stone without disturbing the material it moves through. It leaves no tunnel, no displaced soil, no warning of its passage until it chooses to emerge.
**Tremorsense:** The Sentinel detects all creatures in contact with the ground within 60 feet. The [Hidden] condition does not apply to creatures detected this way, though they still gain the [Concealed] condition against the Sentinel's attacks.
**Siege Monster:** The Sentinel deals double damage to objects and structures.
**Earth Tremor (Recharge 5–8) [Combat]:** Costs 2 actions. The Sentinel drives its fists into the ground, sending violent tremors through the earth in a 60-foot diameter. Every creature on the ground in the area makes a Reflex save (Agi + Luck, opposed by the Sentinel's Con 6 + Wis 3). Creatures that fail take 12 bludgeoning damage (full DR applies — this is physical impact) and gain the Prone condition. Creatures that succeed take no damage. Flying creatures and those not in contact with the ground are unaffected. The Sentinel may use Earth Tremor even while submerged via Earth Glide; when it does, it erupts from the ground as part of the same action.

### Creature Type Traits — Elemental
- Immune to poison damage, Poisoned condition, disease, exhaustion, Paralyzed, Petrified, Unconscious
- Mindless: immune to mind-affecting effects (charm, fear, sleep, psychic effects)
- Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep
 
### Resistances and Vulnerabilities
**Immunities:** Poison damage, Poisoned condition, nonmagical piercing damage, nonmagical slashing damage
**Resistances:** Nonmagical bludgeoning damage — reduce incoming damage by 4 
**Vulnerability:** Thunder damage — the Sentinel takes full damage with no DR reduction from thunder. On any hit that deals thunder damage, it must make a Fortitude save (Con 6 + Luck 2, Easy task — 1 success). On failure, it loses its Earth Glide ability until the start of its next turn as the vibrations disrupt its elemental cohesion.
 
### Description
The Earth Elemental Sentinel is not a creature that hunts. It guards. Something called it here — a nexus, a sacred site, a ward placed by a long-dead mage — and here it remains, patient in the way that stone is patient, which is to say without any awareness that patience is required.
 
It does not distinguish between threats and travelers. Anything that enters the area it protects is a threat. It emerges from the ground with no warning, no posturing, no moment of hesitation before the first slam lands.
 
Scholars who have survived encounters with Sentinels note that they return underground immediately once a threat is neutralized. They do not pursue beyond their ward boundary. They do not take trophies. They do not remember.
 
 
### Tactics
The Sentinel opens from below, using Earth Glide to position directly beneath the most clustered group before emerging and immediately triggering Earth Tremor as part of the same turn. It follows with Multiattack against the nearest standing target, prioritizing whatever is closest rather than identifying priority threats — it does not have the intelligence for threat assessment.
 
Against parties that spread out and avoid clustering, it abandons Earth Tremor and commits to grinding down individual targets with Multiattack, relying on its enormous HP pool and DR to outlast them. Thunder damage forces it above ground and disrupts its preferred tactics significantly; a party that identifies this vulnerability early changes the nature of the encounter entirely.
 
It does not retreat. It does not negotiate. When the ward boundary is breached it responds, and it continues responding until either the threat is gone or it is destroyed.
 
---

## Hag Eye
**Threat Rating:** 2
**Size:** Tiny
**HP:** 28 (Con 2 × 14, Fragile)
**DR:** 0
**Speed:** 50 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 1 / Con 2 / Agi 8 / Dex 6 / Int 3 / Wis 5 / Cha 2 / Luck 3
**Skills:** Melee Combat 0, Perception 5, Stealth 6
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft.
**Initiative Bonus:** +8 (Agi 8)
**Creature Type:** Fae
**Languages:** None spoken. Communicates directly with its creator hag through a shared sensory link.

### Attacks 
The Hag Eye has no meaningful physical attacks. Str 1 renders it incapable of harming anything with its body. Its entire offensive capability is its gaze.

### Special Abilities
**Fae Ancestry:** Fortune on saving throws against charm effects.
**Appendage:** The Hag Eye cannot carry, wear, or manipulate objects of any kind.
**Hag's Sight:** The hag that created this creature sees and hears everything the Hag Eye perceives, regardless of distance, provided both are on the same plane. The hag can close or open this link as a [Free] action on her turn.
**Unnatural Speed:** The Hag Eye's movement does not provoke opportunity attacks. It can move through spaces occupied by other creatures without penalty.
**Withering Gaze (At-Will) [Combat]:** Costs 2 actions. The Hag Eye fixes its gaze on one creature within 60 feet that it can see. The target makes a Will save (Wis + Luck, opposed by the Hag Eye's Wis 5 + Perception 5). On failure, the target suffers one of the following effects chosen by the Hag Eye at the time of the gaze. A creature that succeeds on its save cannot be targeted by Withering Gaze again for the remainder of the encounter.
Each round on the Hag Eye's turn, it may redirect its gaze to a new target as a [Combat] action (2 actions), leaving the previous target's condition in place until that target recovers. A creature can only be under one gaze effect at a time. 
- **Asleep:** The target gains the Unconscious condition. It wakes immediately if it takes any damage or if an adjacent creature spends a [Combat] action to shake it awake.
- **Panicked:** The target gains the Fleeing condition with the Hag Eye as the source of fear. On each of its turns the target must use its full movement to move away from the Hag Eye by the safest available route. If the target reaches a position at least 60 feet from the Hag Eye where it can no longer see it, the effect ends immediately. The target may make a Will save at the end of each of its turns (1 success ends the effect).
- **Sickened:** The target gains the Sickened condition and the Disoriented condition simultaneously. At the end of each of its turns the target may make a Will save (1 success ends both conditions).
 
### Creature Type Traits — Fae
- Fortune on saving throws against charm effects
- Sustained by magical energy rather than food, drink, or sleep
 
### Resistances
**Resistances:** Nonmagical bludgeoning, piercing, and slashing damage — reduce incoming damage of these types by 3.
**Condition Immunities:** Exhaustion, Frightened, Grappled, Prone, Restrained, Stunned, Unconscious. 
The Hag Eye's nature as a detached piece of hag magic makes most physical conditions meaningless. It has no legs to trip, no throat to choke, no mind of its own to terrify.
 
### Description
A Hag Eye is exactly what the name suggests — an eye, plucked from a lesser creature or conjured from hag-magic, animated and sent out into the world as a scout. It moves in silence, leaves no tracks, and reports everything it sees back to the hag who made it.
 
Alone it is nearly harmless in the conventional sense. It cannot lift a stone or open a door. What it can do is look at something in a particular way, and the things it looks at have a tendency to fall asleep, or start running, or feel profoundly unwell.
 
Most parties encounter a Hag Eye and immediately understand the problem: somewhere within range, a hag is watching through it. Destroying the eye is straightforward given its fragility. Finding the hag watching through it is the actual challenge.
 
### Tactics
The Hag Eye avoids direct engagement entirely. It uses its extraordinary Agility and Stealth to position where it can observe the party, feeding information back to its creator while staying out of reach.
 
When forced to act offensively — either because the hag directs it to or because the party is about to reach something the hag wants protected — it prioritizes Asleep on the most dangerous martial threat, then Panicked on whoever is most likely to cause problems while running, then Sickened on spellcasters or anyone left standing. It will not engage a target that has already saved against its gaze.
 
The Hag Eye flees at the first sign it has been spotted. It is nearly impossible to catch at speed 50 with Unnatural Speed preventing opportunity attacks. Ranged attacks and area weaves are the practical options for a party trying to destroy it before it escapes. If the eye is destroyed, the hag loses the sensory link immediately and knows the eye is gone — she does not know how or by whom unless she witnessed it directly.
 
A Hag Eye encountered without its creating hag nearby is either lost, acting on old instructions, or the hag is dead. Any of these situations is worth investigating.

---

## Korsivar
**Threat Rating:** 3
**Size:** Medium
**HP:** 48 (Con 4 × 12, Standard)
**DR:** S: 6, P: 5, B: 4 (Hide)
**Speed:** 35 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 3 / Con 4 / Agi 3 / Dex 4 / Int 2 / Wis 6 / Cha 3 / Luck 3
**Skills:** Melee Combat 3, Perception 5, Stealth 5, Wilderness 5, Medicine 3, Empathy 3
**Senses:** Darkvision 60 ft.
**Initiative Bonus:** +3 (Agi 3)
**Creature Type:** Humanoid
**Background:** Hermit
**Languages:** Common, Hadriaeth

### Attacks
**Staff of the Darach [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 3 + Melee Combat 3), Reach 5 ft.
- ***Margin 1:*** 7 damage (Versatile one-handed: 6 + 1 magic bonus)
- ***Margin 2:*** 10 damage (7 + 3 Str)
- Two-handed:
- ***Margin 1:*** 8 damage (7 + 1 versatile bonus)
- ***Margin 2:*** 11 damage (8 + 3 Str)
The staff is a magic weapon. Attacks with it subtract 1 from the skill die result (the +1 attack bonus).

### Special Abilities
 
**Land's Stride:** Nonmagical difficult terrain costs Korsivar no extra movement. He moves through nonmagical vegetation without penalty regardless of thorns or similar hazards. Fortune on Reflex saves against magically created or manipulated plants.
 
**Mask of the Wild:** Korsivar may attempt to Hide while only lightly obscured by natural phenomena — foliage, rain, snow, mist. He does not need full cover to attempt a Stealth check in natural environments.
 
**Communion with the Wound (1/long rest):** During a short rest, Korsivar communes with the corrupted aspect of nature he serves. He recovers Energy equal to half his Wisdom score (rounded up). This recovery cannot exceed his maximum Energy pool.

### Weaves
**Casting Stat:** Wisdom 6
**Potentials:** Earth 6, Water 5, Positive 4, Negative 4, Space 4, Time 3, Air 3, Fire 2
**Energy Pool:** 42 (sum of potentials + Wis × 2 + Con + mastery ranks ÷ 2)
**Mastery Skills:** Earth 5, Water 4, Positive 3, Negative 3, Space 3, Time 2
**Targeting Roll:** Wisdom + Primary Energy Mastery
 
Korsivar is a Divine Gift caster devoted to a twisted interpretation of Hirnaloyta — not nature as growth and balance but nature as indifferent predation, rot, and reclamation. His patron's Primary energy is Earth (+2) and Secondary is Positive (+1), though he weaponizes both.

| Weave | Energy Cost | Actions | Notes |
|---|---|---|---|
| Thorn vine | Earth 2 | 1 (Simple) | Touch, 4 bludgeoning/piercing |
| Mend Flesh | Positive 3 | 1 (Simple) | Touch only; heals 8 HP |
| Grasping Vines | Earth 3 + Space 6 = 9 | 2 | Medium range, 20 ft. square, Restrained |
| Revealing Light | Positive 2 + Space 6 = 8 | 2 | Outlined, Fortune on attacks against outlined creatures |
| Ice Shard | Water 2 + Space 1 = 3 | 2 | Close range, 8 cold damage |
| Toxic Mist | Negative 2 + Space 1 = 3 | 2 | Close range, 8 poison damage + Poisoned (Weak) |
| Barkward | Earth 4 + Time 2 = 6 | 2 | Touch, +4 DR for 1 minute |
| Shatter | Air 4 + Space 4 = 8 | 2 | Medium range, 10 ft. radius, 16 thunder damage |
| Shadow Sphere | Negative 3 + Space 7 = 10 | 2 | Medium range, 15 ft. radius magical darkness |
| Grasping Vines, Greater | Earth 5 + Space 6 = 11 | 2 | Larger area, more severe restraint; see below |
| Shape Stone | Earth 4 | 1 (Simple) | Touch, permanent reshaping of stone |
 
**Thorn Vine (Simple Weave):** Touch range. Deals 4 piercing damage. On Margin 2, the target is pulled 10 feet directly toward Korsivar.
 
**Grasping Vines, Greater:** Functions as Grasping Vines but in a 30 ft. square at medium range. Restrained creatures that fail a second Reflex save at the start of their turn also gain the Prone condition as the vines drag them down.

 
### Equipment
[[Staff of the Darach]]

### Description

### Tactics
Korsivar does not open fights in the open if he can avoid it. He uses Mask of the Wild and the staff's Verdant Veil to position before combat begins, ideally in natural terrain where he can hide between actions.
 
His opening move is Shadow Sphere dropped on the party's rear — splitting their line of sight and creating chaos — followed immediately by Grasping Vines across the forward group. He then targets isolated or immobilized creatures with Thorn Vine to drag them further out of position while his allies or summoned creatures close in.
 
Barkward goes on himself the moment melee becomes unavoidable, and he will burn staff charges freely to keep his personal Energy pool for offense. He saves Shape Stone for terrain manipulation — blocking exits, trapping individuals, collapsing cover — rather than direct attack.
 
He flees rather than dies. Communion with the Wound means he recovers faster than most, and he treats a tactical retreat as exactly that rather than a defeat. He will be back, better positioned, angrier.

---

## The Swamp Beast
**Threat Rating:** 4
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 156 (Con 6 × 26, Massive)
**DR:** 5 (dense vegetal mass, natural armor)
**Speed:** 20 ft., Swim 20 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 6 / Con 6 / Agi 2 / Dex 2 / Int 1 / Wis 3 / Cha 1 / Luck 2
**Skills:** Melee Combat 6, Stealth 4, Might 5
**Senses:** Blindsight 60 ft. (blind beyond this radius)
**Initiative Bonus:** +2 (Agi 2)
**Creature Type:** Monstrosity
**Languages:** None

### Attacks
**Slam [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 2 + Melee Combat 6), Reach 10 ft. (Large creature)
- ***Margin 1:*** 10 damage (Large, standard natural weapon: 8 + 2)
- ***Margin 2:*** 16 damage (10 + 6 Str)
**Multiattack [Combat]:** The Swamp Beast makes two slam attacks.
- ***Shared Attribute Roll (Agi 2):*** Roll once, apply to both attacks. Roll Melee Combat skill die separately for each.
- ***Engulf Trigger:*** If both slam attacks hit the same Medium or smaller target in the same turn, the Swamp Beast immediately uses Engulf on that target as a [Free] action.
 
### Special Abilities
**Blindsight:** The Swamp Beast perceives its surroundings through vibration and chemical detection within 60 feet. It cannot perceive anything beyond this radius and is effectively blind to it. The [Hidden] condition does not apply to creatures within 60 feet, though they still gain [Concealed] against the Beast's attacks.
**Lightning Absorption:** The Swamp Beast is immune to lightning damage. Whenever it would take lightning damage, it instead regains HP equal to the damage that would have been dealt. This recovery cannot exceed its maximum HP.
**Lightning Surge:** When the Swamp Beast absorbs lightning damage, in addition to recovering HP it gains temporary HP equal to half the absorbed amount (rounded down) until the start of its next turn. These temporary HP are lost at the start of its next turn regardless of whether they were depleted.
**False Appearance:** While the Swamp Beast remains motionless in swamp terrain, it is indistinguishable from a mound of rotting vegetation. A creature that succeeds on a Perception check (Hard task, 2 successes) notices something wrong before the Beast moves.
**Engulf [Free]:** Triggered when both Multiattack slams hit the same Medium or smaller target. The Swamp Beast engulfs the target, drawing it into its mass. The engulfed creature gains the Blinded, Restrained, and Bound conditions simultaneously and cannot breathe.
At the start of each of the Swamp Beast's turns, an engulfed creature makes a Fortitude save (Con + Luck, opposed by the Beast's Con 6 + Wis 3). On failure, the creature takes 12 bludgeoning damage (full DR applies — this is crushing physical force). On success, no damage that turn.
The Swamp Beast can have only one creature engulfed at a time. The engulfed creature moves with the Beast when it moves. To escape, the creature must win an opposed Athletics or Acrobatics check against the Beast's Might 5 + Str 6 on its turn, spending a [Combat] action (2 successes required). An adjacent ally may attempt the same check as a [Combat] action to pull the engulfed creature free.
The engulfed creature is released immediately if the Swamp Beast is reduced to 0 HP.
**Spit Acid (Recharge 5–8) [Combat]:** Costs 2 actions. The Beast expels a stream of acidic fluid in a 15-foot cone. Every creature in the area makes a Reflex save (Agi + Luck, opposed by the Beast's Con 6 + Wis 3). Creatures that fail take 28 acid damage (half DR applies — energy damage). Creatures that succeed take 14 acid damage.

### Resistances and Immunities
**Immunities:** Lightning damage (see Lightning Absorption), Blinded condition, Deafened condition, Exhaustion
**Resistances:** Cold damage and fire damage — reduce incoming damage of these types by 4. The Beast's dense wet mass insulates against both extremes.
**Condition Immunities:** Blinded, Deafened, Exhaustion
 
### Lair Feature — Living Swamp
While the Swamp Beast is in its territory and conscious, the swamp around it responds as an extension of its body. At the start of each round, the Beast may cause one of the following effects without spending any of its actions. Only one effect may be active at a time; triggering a new one ends the previous.
 
- **Grasping Roots:** Up to three roots or vines erupt from the ground at points the Beast can perceive within 60 feet. Each root targets one creature. Each targeted creature makes a Reflex save (Agi + Luck, opposed by the Beast's Might 5 + Con 6). Creatures that fail are Restrained. Each root is a separate object: HP 12, DR 2, immune to poison and psychic damage. A root disappears when reduced to 0 HP, when the Beast triggers a different lair effect, or when the Beast dies. A Restrained creature is released when its root is destroyed.
- **Spore Cloud:** A cloud of toxic spores fills a 20-foot diameter sphere centered on a point the Beast can perceive within 60 feet. The cloud does not move once placed. Every creature in the cloud when it appears makes a Fortitude save (Con + Luck, opposed by the Beast's Con 6 + Wis 3). Creatures that fail take 16 poison damage (half DR applies). Creatures that succeed take 8 poison damage. Any creature that ends its turn inside the cloud takes 8 poison damage automatically with no save. All creatures within the cloud gain the Blinded condition while inside it. The cloud persists until the Beast triggers a different lair effect or dies.
When the Swamp Beast dies, all active lair effects end immediately and the roots collapse.
 
### Description
The Swamp Beast is old enough that the swamp has stopped being its habitat and started being its body. The vines that reach toward intruders are not a separate thing from the creature — they are its nerves, extended outward through the waterlogged soil. The spores it releases are its breath. The acid is the only part that feels like a weapon, and even that is just digestion accelerated.
 
It does not hunt in any meaningful sense. It sits, and things come to it, and when they do it absorbs them. The process is patient and thorough and entirely without malice.
 
What makes it dangerous beyond its raw physical capability is the lightning. Parties that identify its absorption trait and have a mage with a full load of lightning weaves have accidentally created the worst possible situation for themselves — a creature that heals faster than they can damage it through conventional means, now surging with temporary HP and fully alert to the threat.
 
 
### Tactics
The Swamp Beast begins most encounters already in position, motionless and indistinguishable from the surrounding mire. It waits until something comes within 10 feet before erupting.
 
Its priority is Engulf. Every turn it uses Multiattack targeting the same creature, trying to trigger the [Free] Engulf. Once something is engulfed, it ignores that target's allies until they become a more immediate threat, grinding down the engulfed creature with automatic damage each round while slamming anything that gets close.
 
Spit Acid is its only ranged option and it uses it on clustered groups or when melee is temporarily unavailable — not saved, spent when the opportunity presents itself. It has no capacity for tactical patience beyond the initial ambush.
 
The lair's Spore Cloud goes up immediately if the party tries to spread out or stay at range, forcing them to either enter the cloud or cede the terrain. Grasping Roots targets ranged attackers or spellcasters the Beast can perceive through Blindsight, pinning them in place.
 
Against fire or lightning weaves it reacts with something that reads as aggression but is closer to hunger — it moves toward the source of lightning specifically, absorbing what it can and closing to melee range where ranged casters are most vulnerable.
 
It does not retreat. It does not recognize the concept.

---

## Swamp Cat
**Threat Rating:** 2
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 52 (Con 4 × 13, Tough)
**DR:** 2 (natural hide)
**Speed:** 40 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 5 / Con 4 / Agi 4 / Dex 3 / Int 1 / Wis 3 / Cha 2 / Luck 2
**Skills:** Melee Combat 5, Stealth 5, Perception 3
**Senses:** Darkvision 120 ft., Keen Smell
**Initiative Bonus:** +4 (Agi 4)
**Creature Type:** Beast
**Languages:** None

### Attacks
**Bite [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 4 + Melee Combat 5), Reach 5 ft.
- ***Margin 1:*** 10 damage (Large, standard natural weapon: 8 + 2)
- ***Margin 2:*** 15 damage (10 + 5 Str)
**Claw [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 4 + Melee Combat 5), Reach 5 ft.
- ***Margin 1:*** 10 damage (Large, standard natural weapon: 8 + 2)
- ***Margin 2:*** 15 damage (10 + 5 Str)
**Multiattack [Combat]:** The Swamp Cat makes one bite and one claw attack.
- ***Shared Attribute Roll (Agi 4):*** Roll once, apply to both attacks. Roll Melee Combat skill die separately for each.
 
### Special Abilities
**Keen Smell:** Scent-based Perception checks have Fortune.
 
**Pack Tactics:** When an ally is within 5 feet of the target, subtract 1 from both attack dice.
 
**Pounce:** If the Swamp Cat moves at least 20 feet straight toward a target and then hits with a claw attack on the same turn, the target must make a Fortitude save (Con + Luck, opposed by the Cat's Str 5 + Melee Combat 5). On failure, the target gains the Prone condition. If the target is Prone, the Swamp Cat may immediately make one bite attack against it as a [Free] action.
 
### Tactics
Swamp Cats hunt in pairs or small groups, using the terrain to stalk prey before committing to Pounce. Pack Tactics and Pounce together make their opening turn devastating — one cat charges to trigger Prone while the second attacks with subtracted dice against the downed target. They break off if badly wounded, retreating into the swamp to recover.
 
---
 
## Giant Turtle
**Threat Rating:** 2
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 64 (Con 5 × 13, Tough)
**DR:** 8 (shell, natural armor) / 3 while Prone (belly exposed)
**Speed:** 30 ft., Swim 40 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 6 / Con 5 / Agi 2 / Dex 2 / Int 1 / Wis 3 / Cha 1 / Luck 2
**Skills:** Melee Combat 4, Perception 3
**Senses:** Darkvision 60 ft.
**Initiative Bonus:** +2 (Agi 2)
**Creature Type:** Beast
**Languages:** None
 
### Attacks
**Bite [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 2 + Melee Combat 4), Reach 10 ft. (Large creature, long neck)
- ***Margin 1:*** 10 damage (Large, heavy natural weapon: 8 + 2)
- ***Margin 2:*** 16 damage (10 + 6 Str)
 
### Special Abilities
**Amphibious:** The Giant Turtle breathes air and water freely.
 
**Shell Defense:** The Giant Turtle's DR is 8 against all physical attacks while upright. While Prone, its belly is exposed and DR drops to 3 against all damage types.
 
**Stable:** Whenever the Giant Turtle would gain the Prone condition, it makes a Fortitude save (Easy task — 1 success) before the condition applies. On success, the condition is avoided entirely. On failure, the turtle is upside down and cannot right itself without effort — to stand, it must succeed on an Acrobatics check (Hard task — 2 successes) and spend its full movement that turn.
 
**Crushing Bite:** On Margin 2, the target is Grappled in addition to taking damage. While Grappled this way the turtle can maintain the hold without further attack rolls; the target makes an opposed Athletics or Acrobatics check against the Turtle's Might 5 + Str 6 to escape (Hard task — 2 successes).
 
### Tactics
The Giant Turtle is not an aggressive predator. It bites when threatened or when something comes within reach of its neck, and it holds on. Most encounters begin because a party disturbed it. It does not pursue beyond its immediate territory and breaks off if left alone. Flipping it Prone is the tactical priority for any party trying to kill one efficiently — the DR difference between 8 and 3 is the whole fight.

---
 
## Crocodile
**Threat Rating:** 1/2
**Size:** Large
**HP:** 28 (Con 3 × 9, Tough)
**DR:** 2 (scaled hide)
**Speed:** 20 ft., Swim 30 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 4 / Con 3 / Agi 2 / Dex 2 / Int 1 / Wis 2 / Cha 1 / Luck 2
**Skills:** Melee Combat 3, Stealth 3, Perception 2
**Senses:** Normal
**Initiative Bonus:** +2 (Agi 2)
**Creature Type:** Beast
**Languages:** None
 
### Attacks
**Bite [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 2 + Melee Combat 3), Reach 5 ft.
- ***Margin 1:*** 8 damage (Large, standard natural weapon: 8 + 0 — Str does not add at Margin 1)
- ***Margin 2:*** 12 damage (8 + 4 Str)
- ***Special:*** On any hit (Margin 1+), the target is Grappled. While Grappled this way the Crocodile cannot bite a different target. The Grappled creature makes an opposed Athletics or Acrobatics check against the Crocodile's Might 3 + Str 4 to escape (1 success required). If the Bite Grapples a target, Death Roll replaces Bite for all subsequent attacks against that target while the Grapple holds.
**Death Roll [Combat]:** Melee attack against the currently Grappled target only (Agi 2 + Melee Combat 3), Reach 5 ft.
- ***Margin 1:*** 8 damage (Large, standard natural weapon: 8 + 0 — Str does not add at Margin 1)
- ***Margin 2:*** 12 damage (8 + 4 Str)
- ***Special:*** The target makes a Fortitude save (Con + Luck, opposed by the Crocodile's Str 4 + Melee Combat 3). On failure, the target takes an additional 4 damage and gains the Disoriented condition until the end of its next turn. If the target is submerged, it also advances one step along the Drowning condition progression.
 
### Special Abilities
**Hold Breath:** The Crocodile holds its breath for a number of minutes equal to its Constitution score. In combat, this extends to a number of rounds equal to Con × 8 before it must surface.
 
**Swamp Stealth:** In water or swamp terrain, Stealth checks have Fortune.
 
### Tactics
Crocodiles wait submerged with only eyes and nostrils above the waterline, motionless until something comes within reach. The opening bite is everything — if it lands and Grapples, it drags the target into the water and Death Rolls. On land it is slow and commits fully to whatever it has hold of, rarely releasing a target voluntarily. Against armored targets it is far less effective; its damage at Margin 1 is eaten almost entirely by medium armor.
 
---

## Old One Eye
**Threat Rating:** 3
**Size:** Huge
**HP:** 108 (Con 6 × 18, Tough)
**DR:** 3 (scaled hide)
**Speed:** 30 ft., Swim 50 ft.
**Attributes:** Str 6 / Con 6 / Agi 4 / Dex 3 / Int 1 / Wis 4 / Cha 2 / Luck 2
**Skills:** Melee Combat 6, Stealth 6, Perception 5
**Senses:** Normal (one eye — see below)
**Initiative Bonus:** +4 (Agi 4)
**Creature Type:** Beast
**Languages:** None
 
### Attacks
**Bite [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 4 + Melee Combat 6), Reach 10 ft. (Huge creature)
- ***Margin 1:*** 12 damage (Huge, standard natural weapon: 10 + 2)
- ***Margin 2:*** 18 damage (12 + 6 Str)
- ***Special:*** On any hit (Margin 1+), the target is Grappled and Restrained simultaneously. While Grappled this way Old One Eye cannot bite a different target. The Grappled creature makes an opposed Athletics or Acrobatics check against Old One Eye's Might 5 + Str 6 to escape (Hard task — 2 successes).
