**Death Roll [Combat]:** Melee attack against the currently Grappled target only (Agi 4 + Melee Combat 6), Reach 5 ft.
- ***Margin 1:*** 12 damage (Huge, standard natural weapon: 10 + 2)
- ***Margin 2:*** 18 damage (12 + 6 Str)
- ***Special:*** The target makes a Fortitude save (Con + Luck, opposed by Old One Eye's Str 6 + Melee Combat 6). On failure, the target takes an additional 6 damage and gains the Disoriented condition until the end of its next turn. If the target is submerged, it also advances one step along the Drowning condition progression.
**Tail [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 4 + Melee Combat 6), Reach 15 ft. (Huge creature, sweeping tail)
- Can only target creatures not currently Grappled by Old One Eye.
- ***Margin 1:*** 10 damage (Huge, standard natural weapon: 10)
- ***Margin 2:*** 16 damage (10 + 6 Str)
- ***Special:*** On Margin 2, the target makes a Fortitude save (Con + Luck, opposed by Old One Eye's Str 6 + Melee Combat 6). On failure, the target gains the Prone condition.
**Multiattack [Combat]:** Old One Eye makes one bite or death roll attack and one tail attack.
- ***Shared Attribute Roll (Agi 4):*** Roll once, apply to both attacks. Roll Melee Combat skill die separately for each.
- If the bite Grapples a target, the death roll replaces bite in all subsequent turns against that target while the Grapple holds.
 
### Special Abilities
**Hold Breath:** Old One Eye holds its breath for a number of minutes equal to its Constitution score outside of combat. In combat this extends to Con × 8 rounds before it must surface.
 
**One Eye:** Old One Eye lost its left eye long ago to something that did not survive the encounter. It has no peripheral vision on its left side. Attackers approaching or attacking from the left flank subtract 1 from both attack dice against it, as it cannot easily track threats from that direction. Old One Eye's Perception checks relying on sight to the left automatically fail.
 
**Swamp Stealth:** In water or swamp terrain, Stealth checks have Fortune. If Old One Eye is motionless and undetected when combat begins, all creatures that failed to detect it are Surprised on its first turn.
 
**Resistances:** Nonmagical bludgeoning, piercing, and slashing damage — reduce incoming damage of these types by 3.
 
### Description
Old One Eye has lived in the Alderweed longer than anyone can reliably remember. The locals know it is there the way they know the water is cold — as a fact about the environment rather than a threat to be solved. Children are told to stay away from the deep channels. Most of them listen.
 
The missing eye is the only way to distinguish it from the water itself when it lies still. It does not patrol or hunt with any visible strategy. It simply occupies the swamp, and things that come within range of its jaws stop being a concern.
 
Whatever took its eye left scars that run from the empty socket to the back of its jaw. The scars are old enough that the scales have grown back over them in ridges. Scholars who have seen the marks and survived the encounter suggest the wound came from another predator of significant size. No one has confirmed what kind.
 
### Tactics
 
Old One Eye's entire strategy is the ambush. It lies motionless below the waterline using Swamp Stealth, sometimes for hours, until something comes close enough. The first round is usually decisive — Surprised targets cannot defend, and a Huge creature biting through light armor and immediately beginning Death Roll on the Grappled target while its tail sweeps anyone trying to intervene is genuinely dangerous to a Tier 2–3 party.
 
Once it has something in its jaws it does not let go. Death Roll replaces Bite every subsequent turn against the Grappled target, grinding through HP while the tail handles anyone approaching to help. It ignores threats it cannot reach rather than releasing its current target — creatures more than 15 feet away are simply not its problem until the thing in its mouth stops moving.
 
Its left side is the tactical opening. A coordinated party that positions fighters on Old One Eye's blind flank while a second threat occupies its attention from the right forces it into a choice it does not have the intelligence to resolve well. It will focus on whichever target it already has hold of and trust its DR to absorb what it cannot see coming.
 
It retreats into deep water when reduced below 40 HP, holding its breath and sinking to the bottom. It will not resurface while threats remain visible. Whether the party has the means and the will to follow it down is the question that ends most encounters with Old One Eye.

---

## Haunt
**Threat Rating:** 3
**Size:** Medium
**HP:** 72 (Con 4 × 18, Standard Undead)
**DR:** 0 (incorporeal — physical DR does not apply; see Resistances)
**Speed:** 0 ft., Fly 30 ft. (Hover)
**Attributes:** Str 3 / Con 4 / Agi 5 / Dex 4 / Int 4 / Wis 5 / Cha 4 / Luck 3
**Skills:** Melee Combat 4, Perception 5, Stealth 5, Arcane 3
**Senses:** Blindsight 30 ft., Darkvision 60 ft. (including magical darkness)
**Initiative Bonus:** +5 (Agi 5)
**Creature Type:** Undead
**Languages:** Understands Elven (Hadriaeth). Cannot speak.

### Attacks
**Life Drain [Combat]:** Melee attack (Agi 5 + Melee Combat 4), Reach 5 ft.
- ***Margin 1:*** 8 necrotic damage (half DR applies). The target's maximum HP is reduced by 8. Current HP is unaffected unless it now exceeds the new maximum, in which case reduce current HP to the new maximum.
- ***Margin 2:*** 11 necrotic damage (8 + 3 Str). The target's maximum HP is reduced by 11.

Maximum HP lost to Life Drain restores fully after a long rest. Any magical healing that restores HP simultaneously restores an equal amount of lost maximum HP up to the total drained. A target whose maximum HP is reduced to 0 dies.

### Special Abilities
**Undead Traits:**
- Immune to poison damage, Poisoned condition, disease, exhaustion
- Immune to the Charmed, Grappled, Paralyzed, Petrified, Prone, Restrained, and Unconscious conditions
- Does not need air, food, drink, or sleep
- Mindless immunity does not apply — the Haunt retains intelligence and volition

**Incorporeal Movement:** The Haunt moves through other creatures and objects as if they were difficult terrain. It takes 4 force damage if it ends its turn inside an object.

**Sunlight Sensitivity:** While in direct sunlight, the Haunt has Misfortune on attack rolls and on Perception checks that rely on sight.

**Frightful Presence (3/day) [Combat]:** Costs 1 action. Every creature of the Haunt's choice within 30 feet that can see it makes a Will save (Wis + Luck, opposed by the Haunt's Cha 4 + Perception 5). Creatures that fail gain the Frightened condition for 1 minute with the Haunt as the source. They may repeat the save at the end of each of their turns (1 success ends the effect). A creature that succeeds on its save, or recovers from the condition, cannot be affected by this Haunt's Frightful Presence for 24 hours.

**Silver and Magic:** Nonmagical, non-silver weapons deal no damage to the Haunt. Magical weapons and silver weapons deal damage normally. This is not a DR reduction — nonmagical non-silver damage simply does not register.

### Resistances and Immunities

**Immunities:** Necrotic damage, poison damage, nonmagical non-silver bludgeoning, nonmagical non-silver piercing, nonmagical non-silver slashing

**Resistances:** Acid, cold, fire, lightning, and thunder damage — reduce incoming damage of these types by 4. Magical and silver bludgeoning, piercing, and slashing — reduce incoming damage by 4.

### Weaves
**Casting Stat:** Wisdom 5
**Targeting Roll:** Wisdom + primary Energy Mastery

The Haunt does not channel magic through study or faith. Its weaves are the residue of whatever it was in life, leaking outward as instinct. It cannot explain what it does. It simply does it.

| Weave | Energy | Actions | Frequency |
|---|---|---|---|
| Fog Cloud | Air 2 + Space 4 = 6 | 2 | At will |
| Invisibility | Space 4 + Time 3 = 7 | 2 | At will |
| Minor Illusion | Space 3 + Time 2 = 5 | 2 | At will |
| Phantom Image | Space 4 + Time 2 = 6 | 2 | At will |
| Complex Illusion | Space 6 + Time 3 = 9 | 2 | 1/encounter |

**Energy Pool:** 32. The Haunt's pool does not recover mid-encounter. Its at-will designation reflects that these weaves are cheap enough relative to its pool that it can cast them freely across a standard encounter without running dry — not that they cost nothing.

**Fog Cloud:** Creates a heavily obscured sphere 40 feet diameter at medium range (60 ft.). All creatures inside gain the Concealed condition against all attackers. The Haunt can see through its own fog using Blindsight within 30 feet.

**Invisibility:** The Haunt gains the Hidden condition. The effect ends if it takes a [Combat] action or casts a weave other than Fog Cloud, which it can maintain while invisible since Fog Cloud requires no ongoing action to sustain once placed.

**Minor Illusion and Phantom Image:** Function as written in the weave list. The Haunt uses these to create sounds, figures, and movement — a voice from the wrong direction, the shape of something familiar in the fog, footsteps retreating down a corridor that has no exit.

### Description
A Haunt is what remains when something died with unfinished business and the pneuma could not let go. It understands Elven but cannot speak — whatever part of its former self held language is gone. What remains is hunger, patience, and the specific kind of cunning that belongs to predators that have been hunting the same territory for a very long time.

It does not attack immediately. It watches. The fog goes up first, then the illusions start — sounds that don't match their apparent sources, shapes glimpsed at the edge of torchlight, the sense that something is just behind you in a room you know is empty. By the time a creature realizes what is happening, the Haunt is already within reach.

What it wants is unclear. The life drain suggests sustenance, but the Haunt does not seem to need it the way living things need food. It may simply be habit — the echo of something it did in life, continuing past the point where life gave it meaning.

### Tactics
The Haunt opens at range, placing Fog Cloud to fragment the party and eliminate sightlines. It then uses Invisibility and moves into the fog where its Blindsight functions and the party's vision does not. Phantom Image and Minor Illusion run simultaneously to pull individual creatures away from the group — a familiar voice, a figure retreating into the dark, the sound of someone calling for help from the wrong direction.

Once a target is isolated the Haunt uses Frightful Presence before closing to Life Drain range. A Frightened creature trying to flee has already moved away from its allies. The Haunt follows, draining maximum HP with each hit, and retreats back into the fog before the rest of the party can respond.

It prioritizes one target at a time and does not switch until that target is dead or the tactical situation forces it.

Sunlight is its only reliable deterrent. A party that can create or sustain a Magical Radiant Light effect of sufficient energy inside the fog forces the Haunt to disengage or fight at Misfortune — its preferred environment stops being safe. It will withdraw rather than fight on those terms, returning when the light source expires.

Silver weapons and magical attacks are the only physical options. A party without either cannot damage it through conventional means and should treat the encounter as a puzzle rather than a fight until they find another approach.
